<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Prejudicial treatment based on membership in a certain group</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the prejudicial treatment. For the ability to distinguish one thing from another, see <a href="/wiki/Discrimination_(information)" title="Discrimination (information)">Discrimination (information)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note"><span>Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Discriminant" title="Discriminant">discriminant</a>.</span> <span>"Bigot" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Bigot_(disambiguation)" title="Bigot (disambiguation)">Bigot (disambiguation)</a>.</span></div>

</div></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Discrimination_sidebar" title="Template:Discrimination sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Discrimination_sidebar" title="Template talk:Discrimination sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Discrimination_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Discrimination</b> is the act of making unjustified distinctions between people based on the groups, classes, or other categories to which they belong or are perceived to belong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> People may be discriminated on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Racial_discrimination" title="Racial discrimination">race</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">gender</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religious_discrimination" title="Religious discrimination">religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ableism" title="Ableism">disability</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation_discrimination" title="Sexual orientation discrimination">sexual orientation</a>, as well as other categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apa-discrimination_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-apa-discrimination-2">[2]</a></sup> Discrimination especially occurs when individuals or groups are unfairly treated in a way which is worse than other people are treated, on the basis of their actual or perceived membership in certain groups or social categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apa-discrimination_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-apa-discrimination-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> It involves restricting members of one group from opportunities or privileges that are available to members of another group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>Discriminatory traditions, policies, ideas, practices and laws exist in many countries and <a href="/wiki/Institution" title="Institution">institutions</a> in all parts of the world, including territories where discrimination is generally looked down upon. In some places, attempts such as quotas have been used to benefit those who are believed to be current or past victims of discrimination. These attempts have often been met with controversy, and have sometimes been called <a href="/wiki/Reverse_discrimination" title="Reverse discrimination">reverse discrimination</a>.
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The term <i>discriminate</i> appeared in the early 17th century in the English language. It is from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a> <i>discriminat-</i> 'distinguished between', from the verb <i>discriminare</i>, from <i>discrimen</i> 'distinction', from the verb <i>discernere</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> the term "discrimination" generally evolved in <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a> usage as an understanding of prejudicial treatment of an individual based solely on their race, later generalized as membership in a certain socially undesirable <a href="/wiki/Social_group" title="Social group">group</a> or social category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> 
Before this sense of the word became almost universal, it was a synonym for discernment, tact and culture as in "taste and discrimination", generally a laudable attribute; to "discriminate against" being commonly disparaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Moral philosophers have defined discrimination using a <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">moralized</a> definition. Under this approach, discrimination is defined as acts, practices, or policies that wrongfully impose a relative disadvantage or deprivation on persons based on their membership in a salient social group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> This is a comparative definition. An individual need not be actually harmed in order to be discriminated against. He or she just needs to be treated <i>worse</i> than others for some arbitrary reason. If someone decides to donate to help orphan children, but decides to donate less, say, to black children out of a racist attitude, he or she will be acting in a discriminatory way even if he or she actually benefits the people he discriminates against by donating some money to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Discrimination also develops into a source of <a href="/wiki/Oppression" title="Oppression">oppression</a>, the action of recognizing someone as 'different' so much that they are treated inhumanly and degraded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>This moralized definition of discrimination is distinct to a non-moralized definition - in the former, discrimination is wrong by definition, whereas in the latter, this is not the case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altman_2020_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Altman_2020-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> stance on discrimination includes the statement: "Discriminatory behaviors take many forms, but they all involve some form of exclusion or rejection."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> and other international bodies work towards helping ending discrimination around the world.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_discrimination">Types of discrimination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Types of discrimination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Age">Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">Ageism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adultism" title="Adultism">Adultism</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">Ageism</a> or age discrimination is discrimination and stereotyping based on the grounds of someone's age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> It is a set of beliefs, norms, and values which used to justify discrimination or subordination based on a person's age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KirkpatrickKatsiaficas1987_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-KirkpatrickKatsiaficas1987-15">[15]</a></sup> Ageism is most often directed toward elderly people, or adolescents and children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>Age discrimination in hiring has been shown to exist in the United States. Joanna Lahey, professor at The Bush School of Government and Public Service at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M" title="Texas A&amp;M">Texas A&amp;M</a>, found that firms are more than 40% more likely to interview a young adult job applicant than an older job applicant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In Europe, Stijn Baert, Jennifer Norga, Yannick Thuy and Marieke Van Hecke, researchers at <a href="/wiki/Ghent_University" title="Ghent University">Ghent University</a>, measured comparable ratios in Belgium. They found that age discrimination is heterogeneous by the activity older candidates undertook during their additional post-educational years. In Belgium, they are only discriminated if they have more years of inactivity or irrelevant employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a survey for the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kent" title="University of Kent">University of Kent</a>, England, 29% of respondents stated that they had suffered from age discrimination. This is a higher proportion than for <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">gender</a> or <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racial</a> discrimination. <a href="/wiki/Dominic_Abrams" title="Dominic Abrams">Dominic Abrams</a>, social psychology professor at the university, concluded that ageism is the most pervasive form of <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudice</a> experienced in the UK population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Caste">Caste</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Caste">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">Caste</a></div>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">caste</a> discrimination affects an estimated 250 million people worldwide and is mainly prevalent in parts of Asia (India, Sri Lanka, Bangladesh, Pakistan, Nepal, Japan) and Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 200 million <a href="/wiki/Dalit" title="Dalit">Dalits</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scheduled_Castes" title="Scheduled Castes">Scheduled Castes</a> (formerly known as "untouchables") in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disability">Disability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Disability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disability_discrimination" title="Disability discrimination">Disability discrimination</a></div>
<p>Discrimination against people with <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disabilities</a> in favor of people who are not is called <a href="/wiki/Ableism" title="Ableism">ableism</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disablism" title="Disablism">disablism</a>. Disability discrimination, which treats non-disabled individuals as the standard of 'normal living', results in public and private places and services, educational settings, and social services that are built to serve 'standard' people, thereby excluding those with various disabilities. Studies have shown that disabled people not only need employment in order to be provided with the opportunity to earn a living but they also need employment in order to sustain their mental health and well-being. Work fulfils a number of basic needs for an individual such as collective purpose, social contact, status, and activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> A person with a disability is often found to be socially isolated and work is one way to reduce his or her isolation.
</p><p>In the United States, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Americans_with_Disabilities_Act" title="Americans with Disabilities Act">Americans with Disabilities Act</a> mandates the provision of equality of access to both buildings and services and is paralleled by similar acts in other countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/Equality_Act_2010" title="Equality Act 2010">Equality Act 2010</a> in the UK.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corsican_nationalism.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Corsican_nationalism.jpg/220px-Corsican_nationalism.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Corsican_nationalism.jpg/330px-Corsican_nationalism.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Corsican_nationalism.jpg/440px-Corsican_nationalism.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corsican_nationalism.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nationalists in <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> sometimes spray-paint or shoot traffic signs in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref" role="note">This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_discrimination" title="Linguistic discrimination">Linguistic discrimination</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Linguistic_discrimination&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Linguistic_discrimination" title="Linguistic discrimination">Linguistic discrimination</a> (also called glottophobia, linguicism and languagism) is unfair treatment of people which is based on <a href="/wiki/Usage_(language)" title="Usage (language)">their use of language</a> and the characteristics of their speech, including their <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a>, their <a href="/wiki/Accent_(sociolinguistics)" title="Accent (sociolinguistics)">accent</a>, the perceived size of their <a href="/wiki/Vocabulary" title="Vocabulary">vocabulary</a> (whether or not the speaker uses complex and varied words), their <a href="/wiki/Modality_(semiotics)" title="Modality (semiotics)">modality</a>, and their <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">syntax</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> For example, an <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan speaker</a> in France will probably be treated differently from a <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French speaker</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Linguistic_discrimination_aclunc.org_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Linguistic_discrimination_aclunc.org-26">[26]</a></sup> Based on a difference in use of language, a person may automatically form judgments about another person's <a href="/wiki/Wealth" title="Wealth">wealth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_status" title="Social status">social status</a>, character or other traits, which may lead to discrimination.
</p><p>In the mid-1980s, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linguist" title="Linguist">linguist</a> <a href="/wiki/Tove_Skutnabb-Kangas" title="Tove Skutnabb-Kangas">Tove Skutnabb-Kangas</a> captured the idea of language-based discrimination as linguicism, which was defined as "ideologies and structures which are used to legitimize, effectuate, and reproduce unequal divisions of power and resources (both material and non-material) between groups which are defined on the basis of language".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Although different names have been given to this form of discrimination, they all hold the same definition. It is also important to note that linguistic discrimination is culturally and socially determined due to preference for one use of language over others.
</p>
Scholars have analyzed the role of <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_imperialism" title="Linguistic imperialism">linguistic imperialism</a> in linguicism, with some asserting that speakers of dominant languages gravitate towards discrimination against speakers of other, less dominant languages, while disadvantaging themselves linguistically by remaining monolingual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Linguistic_discrimination_TBD1_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Linguistic_discrimination_TBD1-28">[28]</a></sup> According to scholar Carolyn McKinley, this phenomenon is most present in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, where the majority of the population speaks <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Europe" title="Languages of Europe">European languages</a> introduced during the <a href="/wiki/Colonisation_of_Africa" title="Colonisation of Africa">colonial era</a>; African states are also noted as instituting European languages as the main medium of instruction, instead of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_language" title="Indigenous language">indigenous languages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Linguistic_discrimination_TBD1_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Linguistic_discrimination_TBD1-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> reports have noted that this has historically benefitted only the African <a href="/wiki/Upper_class" title="Upper class">upper class</a>, conversely disadvantaging the majority of Africa's population who hold varying level of fluency in the European languages spoken across the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Linguistic_discrimination_TBD1_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-Linguistic_discrimination_TBD1-28">[28]</a></sup> Scholars have also noted impact of the linguistic dominance of English on <a href="/wiki/Academic_discipline" title="Academic discipline">academic discipline</a>; scholar Anna Wierzbicka has described disciplines such as <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> being "locked in a conceptual framework grounded in English" which prevents academia as a whole from reaching a "more universal, culture-independent perspective".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Linguistic_discrimination_:1_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Linguistic_discrimination_:1-29">[29]</a></sup></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Discrimination based on a person's name may also occur, with researchers suggesting that this form of discrimination is present based on a name's meaning, its pronunciation, its uniqueness, its gender affiliation, and its racial affiliation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Research has further shown that real world recruiters spend an average of just six seconds reviewing each résumé before making their initial "fit/no fit" screen-out decision and that a person's name is one of the six things they focus on most.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> France has made it illegal to view a person's name on a résumé when screening for the initial list of most qualified candidates. Great Britain, Germany, Sweden, and the Netherlands have also experimented with name-blind summary processes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Some apparent discrimination may be explained by other factors such as name frequency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The effects of name discrimination based on a name's fluency is subtle, small and subject to significantly changing norms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nationality">Nationality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Nationality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Discrimination on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Nationality" title="Nationality">nationality</a> is usually included in <a href="/wiki/Employment_discrimination" title="Employment discrimination">employment laws</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> (see above <a href="#Employment">section for employment discrimination</a> specifically). It is sometimes referred to as bound together with racial discrimination<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> although it can be separate. It may vary from laws that stop refusals of hiring based on nationality, asking questions regarding origin, to prohibitions of firing, forced retirement, compensation and pay, etc., based on nationality.
</p><p>Discrimination on the basis of nationality may show as a "level of acceptance" in a sport or work team regarding new team members and employees who differ from the nationality of the majority of team members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">GCC</a> states, in the workplace, preferential treatment is given to full citizens, even though many of them lack experience or motivation to do the job. State benefits are also generally available for citizens only.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Westerners might also get paid more than other expatriates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_or_ethnicity">Race or ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Race or ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">Racism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racial_discrimination" title="Racial discrimination">Racial discrimination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Discrimination_based_on_skin_color" title="Discrimination based on skin color">Discrimination based on skin color</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_penalty" title="Ethnic penalty">Ethnic penalty</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">Racial segregation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anti_Arab_sign_in_Pattaya_Beach_Thailand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="511" data-file-width="886" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Anti_Arab_sign_in_Pattaya_Beach_Thailand.jpg/220px-Anti_Arab_sign_in_Pattaya_Beach_Thailand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Anti_Arab_sign_in_Pattaya_Beach_Thailand.jpg/330px-Anti_Arab_sign_in_Pattaya_Beach_Thailand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Anti_Arab_sign_in_Pattaya_Beach_Thailand.jpg/440px-Anti_Arab_sign_in_Pattaya_Beach_Thailand.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anti_Arab_sign_in_Pattaya_Beach_Thailand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Anti-Arabism" title="Anti-Arabism">Anti-Arab</a> sign in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pattaya_Beach" title="Pattaya Beach">Pattaya Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:No_entrance_for_poles1.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="282" data-file-width="420" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/No_entrance_for_poles1.jpeg/220px-No_entrance_for_poles1.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/No_entrance_for_poles1.jpeg/330px-No_entrance_for_poles1.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e5/No_entrance_for_poles1.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:No_entrance_for_poles1.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>German warning in <a href="/wiki/German-occupied_Poland" title="German-occupied Poland">German-occupied Poland</a> 1939 – "<a href="/wiki/Nur_f%C3%BCr_Deutsche" title="Nur für Deutsche">No entrance for Poles</a>!"</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:37431682_eb5832e644.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/37431682_eb5832e644.jpg/220px-37431682_eb5832e644.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/37431682_eb5832e644.jpg/330px-37431682_eb5832e644.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/37431682_eb5832e644.jpg/440px-37431682_eb5832e644.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:37431682_eb5832e644.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Racial_antisemitism" title="Racial antisemitism">Antisemitic</a> graffiti in <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>. The words read <i>Juden raus</i> (German for <i>Jews out</i>) and <i>Hasse</i> (presumably a misspelling of <i>Hass</i>, German for <i>hate</i>)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Segregation_1938b.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2139" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Segregation_1938b.jpg/250px-Segregation_1938b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Segregation_1938b.jpg/375px-Segregation_1938b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Segregation_1938b.jpg/500px-Segregation_1938b.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Segregation_1938b.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> child at a segregated drinking fountain on a courthouse lawn, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, US 1938.</div></div></div>
<p>Racial and ethnic discrimination differentiates individuals on the basis of real and perceived racial and ethnic differences and leads to various forms of the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_penalty" title="Ethnic penalty">ethnic penalty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carmichael_&amp;_woods,_2000_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-carmichael_&amp;_woods,_2000-45">[45]</a></sup> It can also refer to the belief that groups of humans possess different behavioral traits corresponding to physical appearance and can be divided based on the <a href="/wiki/Supremacism" title="Supremacism">superiority</a> of one <a href="/wiki/Race_(human_categorization)" title="Race (human categorization)">race</a> over another.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxforddictionaries.com_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-oxforddictionaries.com-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghani_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ghani-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newman,_D.M._49-0"><a href="#cite_note-newman,_D.M.-49">[49]</a></sup> It may also mean <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudice</a>, discrimination, or antagonism directed against other people because they are of a different race or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnicity" title="Ethnicity">ethnicity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxforddictionaries.com_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-oxforddictionaries.com-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghani_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ghani-48">[48]</a></sup> Modern variants of <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> are often based in social perceptions of biological differences between peoples. These views can take the form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_actions" title="Social actions">social actions</a>, practices or beliefs, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_systems" title="Political systems">political systems</a> in which different races are ranked as inherently superior or inferior to each other, based on presumed shared inheritable traits, abilities, or qualities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxforddictionaries.com_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-oxforddictionaries.com-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ghani_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ghani-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newman_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-newman-50">[50]</a></sup> It has been official government policy in several countries, such as <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> era. Discriminatory policies towards ethnic minorities include the race-based discrimination against ethnic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaysian_Indian" title="Malaysian Indian">Indians</a> and Chinese in Malaysia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, many <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_boat_people" title="Vietnamese boat people">Vietnamese</a> <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a> moved to Australia and the United States, where they face discrimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Region">Region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Regional_discrimination_in_China" title="Regional discrimination in China">Regional discrimination in China</a></div>
<p>Regional or geographic discrimination is a form of discrimination that is based on the region in which a person lives or the region in which a person was born. It differs from national discrimination because it may not be based on national borders or the country in which the victim lives, instead, it is based on prejudices against a specific region of one or more countries. Examples include discrimination against Chinese people who were born in regions of the countryside that are far away from cities that are located within China, and discrimination against <a href="/wiki/Americans" title="Americans">Americans</a> who are from the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">southern</a> or <a href="/wiki/Northern_United_States" title="Northern United States">northern</a> regions of the United States. It is often accompanied by discrimination that is based on accent, dialect, or cultural differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Accent_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Accent-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_beliefs">Religious beliefs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Religious beliefs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religious_discrimination" title="Religious discrimination">Religious discrimination</a></div>

<a href="/wiki/Portal:Religion" title="Portal:Religion">Religion portal</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Religious_freedom" title="Template:Religious freedom"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Religious_freedom" title="Template talk:Religious freedom"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Religious_freedom&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="892" data-file-width="1383" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg/220px-Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg/330px-Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg/440px-Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lotshampa_refugees_in_Beldangi_Camp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the 1990s, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_refugees" title="Bhutanese refugees">expelled its Hindu population or forced it to leave the country</a> in order to preserve Bhutan's Buddhist culture and identity.</div></div></div>
<p>Religious discrimination is valuing or treating people or groups differently because of what they do or do not believe in or because of their feelings towards a given <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>. For instance, the Jewish population of Germany, and indeed a large portion of Europe, was subjected to discrimination under <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> and his Nazi party between 1933 and 1945. They were forced to live in ghettos, wear an identifying star of David on their clothes, and sent to concentration and death camps in rural Germany and Poland, where they were to be tortured and killed, all because of their Jewish religion. Many laws (most prominently the Nuremberg Laws of 1935) separated those of Jewish faith as supposedly inferior to the Christian population.
</p><p>Restrictions on the types of occupations that <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> people could hold were imposed by Christian authorities. Local rulers and church officials closed many professions to religious Jews, pushing them into marginal roles that were considered socially inferior, such as tax and rent collecting and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moneylending" title="Moneylending">moneylending</a>, occupations that were only tolerated as a "<a href="/wiki/Necessary_evil" title="Necessary evil">necessary evil</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The number of Jews who were permitted to reside in different places was limited; they were concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Ghetto" title="Ghetto">ghettos</a> and banned from owning land. In Saudi Arabia, non-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> are not allowed to publicly practice their religions and they cannot enter <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medina" title="Medina">Medina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mackeymecca_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-mackeymecca-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-56">[56]</a></sup> Furthermore, private non-Muslim religious gatherings might be raided by the <a href="/wiki/Religious_police" title="Religious police">religious police</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-56">[56]</a></sup> In Maldives, non-Muslims living and visiting the country are prohibited from openly expressing their religious beliefs, holding public congregations to conduct religious activities, or involving Maldivians in such activities. Those expressing religious beliefs other than Islam may face imprisonment of up to five years or house arrest, fines ranging from 5,000 to 20,000 rufiyaa ($320 to $1,300), and deportation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 1979 consultation on the issue, the United States commission on civil rights defined religious discrimination in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Civil_and_political_rights" title="Civil and political rights">civil rights</a> which are guaranteed by the <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Fourteenth Amendment</a>. Whereas religious civil liberties, such as the right to hold or not to hold a religious belief, are essential for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_of_Religion" title="Freedom of Religion">Freedom of Religion</a> (in the United States as secured by the <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First Amendment</a>), religious discrimination occurs when someone is denied "equal protection under the law, equality of status under the law, equal treatment in the administration of justice, and equality of opportunity and access to employment, education, housing, public services and facilities, and public accommodation because of their exercise of their right to religious freedom".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Sex.2C_sex_characteristics.2C_gender.2C_and_gender_identity"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sex,_sex_characteristics,_gender,_and_gender_identity">Sex, sex characteristics, gender, and gender identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sex, sex characteristics, gender, and gender identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">Sexism</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">Homophobia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Misogyny" title="Misogyny">Misogyny</a>, <a href="/wiki/Misandry" title="Misandry">Misandry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Discrimination_against_intersex_people" title="Discrimination against intersex people">Discrimination against intersex people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transphobia" title="Transphobia">Transphobia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discrimination_towards_non-binary_gender_persons" title="Discrimination towards non-binary gender persons">Discrimination towards non-binary gender persons</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_LGBT_people" title="Violence against LGBT people">Violence against LGBT people</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">Sexism</a> is a form of discrimination based on a person's sex or gender. It has been linked to <a href="/wiki/Stereotype" title="Stereotype">stereotypes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gender_role" title="Gender role">gender roles</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and may include the belief that one sex or gender is intrinsically superior to another.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0a_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0a-61">[61]</a></sup> Extreme sexism may foster <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">sexual harassment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a>, and other forms of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Gender discrimination may encompass sexism and is discrimination toward people based on their <a href="/wiki/Gender_identity" title="Gender identity">gender identity</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macklem_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Macklem-63">[63]</a></sup> or their gender or sex differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lenhart_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lenhart-64">[64]</a></sup> Gender discrimination is especially defined in terms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Workplace_inequality" title="Workplace inequality">workplace inequality</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lenhart_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lenhart-64">[64]</a></sup> It may arise from social or cultural customs and norms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Intersex" title="Intersex">Intersex</a> persons experience <a href="/wiki/Discrimination_against_intersex_people" title="Discrimination against intersex people">discrimination</a> due to innate, atypical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sex_characteristics" title="Sex characteristics">sex characteristics</a>. Multiple jurisdictions now protect individuals on grounds of <i>intersex status</i> or <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sex_characteristics" title="Sex characteristics">sex characteristics</a></i>. South Africa was the first country to explicitly add intersex to legislation, as part of the attribute of 'sex'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Australia was the first country to add an independent attribute, of 'intersex status'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expmem_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-expmem-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Malta was the first to adopt a broader framework of 'sex characteristics', through legislation that also ended modifications to the sex characteristics of minors undertaken for social and cultural reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gate-malta_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-gate-malta-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oiieu-malta_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-oiieu-malta-70">[70]</a></sup> Global efforts such as the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_5" title="Sustainable Development Goal 5">Sustainable Development Goal 5</a> is also aimed at ending all forms of discrimination on the basis of gender and sex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_orientation">Sexual orientation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sexual orientation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cologne_Germany_Cologne-Gay-Pride-2015_Parade-17b.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="4969" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Cologne_Germany_Cologne-Gay-Pride-2015_Parade-17b.jpg/220px-Cologne_Germany_Cologne-Gay-Pride-2015_Parade-17b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Cologne_Germany_Cologne-Gay-Pride-2015_Parade-17b.jpg/330px-Cologne_Germany_Cologne-Gay-Pride-2015_Parade-17b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Cologne_Germany_Cologne-Gay-Pride-2015_Parade-17b.jpg/440px-Cologne_Germany_Cologne-Gay-Pride-2015_Parade-17b.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cologne_Germany_Cologne-Gay-Pride-2015_Parade-17b.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>LGBT activists at <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Pride" title="Cologne Pride">Cologne Pride</a> carrying a banner with the flags of over 70 countries where <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_by_country_or_territory" title="LGBT rights by country or territory">homosexuality is illegal</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg/220px-Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg/330px-Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg/440px-Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protests in New York City against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill" title="Uganda Anti-Homosexuality Bill">Uganda's Anti-Homosexuality Bill</a>.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Heterosexism" title="Heterosexism">Heterosexism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heteronormativity" title="Heteronormativity">Heteronormativity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biphobia" title="Biphobia">Biphobia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">Homophobia</a></div>
<p>One's sexual orientation is a "predilection for homosexuality, heterosexuality, or bisexuality".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Like most minority groups, homosexuals and bisexuals are vulnerable to prejudice and discrimination from the majority group. They may experience hatred from others because of their sexuality; a term for such hatred based upon one's sexual orientation is often called <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">homophobia</a>. Many continue to hold negative feelings towards those with non-heterosexual orientations and will discriminate against people who have them or are thought to have them. People of other uncommon sexual orientations also experience discrimination. One study found its sample of heterosexuals to be more prejudiced against <a href="/wiki/Asexuality" title="Asexuality">asexual people</a> than against homosexual or bisexual people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Employment_discrimination" title="Employment discrimination">Employment discrimination</a> based on sexual orientation varies by country. Revealing a lesbian sexual orientation (by means of mentioning an engagement in a rainbow organisation or by mentioning one's partner name) lowers employment opportunities in <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and Greece but overall, it has no negative effect in Sweden and Belgium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In the latter country, even a positive effect of revealing a lesbian sexual orientation is found for women at their fertile ages.
</p><p>Besides these academic studies, in 2009, <a href="/wiki/International_Lesbian,_Gay,_Bisexual,_Trans_and_Intersex_Association" title="International Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual, Trans and Intersex Association">ILGA</a> published a report based on research carried out by Daniel Ottosson at Södertörn University College, Stockholm, Sweden. This research found that of the 80 countries around the world that continue to consider <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> illegal, five carry the <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">death penalty</a> for homosexual activity, and two do in some regions of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In the report, this is described as "State sponsored homophobia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> This happens in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Islamic</a> states, or in two cases regions under Islamic authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> On February 5, 2005, the <a href="/wiki/The_New_Humanitarian" title="The New Humanitarian">IRIN</a> issued a reported titled "Iraq: Male homosexuality still a taboo". The article stated, among other things that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honor_killings" title="Honor killings">honor killings</a> by Iraqis against a gay family member are common and given some legal protection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> In August 2009, Human Rights Watch published an extensive report detailing torture of men accused of being <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Iraq" title="LGBT rights in Iraq">gay in Iraq</a>, including the blocking of men's anuses with glue and then giving the men laxatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Although gay marriage has been legal in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> since 2006, same-sex unions are often condemned as "un-African".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Research conducted in 2009 shows 86% of black lesbians from the <a href="/wiki/Western_Cape" title="Western Cape">Western Cape</a> live in fear of sexual assault.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_by_country_or_territory" title="LGBT rights by country or territory">LGBT rights by country or territory</a></div>
<p>A number of countries, especially those in the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>, have passed measures to alleviate discrimination against sexual minorities, including laws against anti-gay <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hate_crimes" title="Hate crimes">hate crimes</a> and workplace discrimination. Some have also legalized same-sex marriage or civil unions in order to grant same-sex couples the same protections and benefits as opposite-sex couples. In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> passed its first resolution recognizing LGBT rights.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reverse_discrimination">Reverse discrimination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reverse discrimination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reverse_discrimination" title="Reverse discrimination">Reverse discrimination</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bumiputera_(Malaysia)" title="Bumiputera (Malaysia)">Bumiputera (Malaysia)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Protesto_contra_o_sistema_de_cotas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1311" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Protesto_contra_o_sistema_de_cotas.jpg/170px-Protesto_contra_o_sistema_de_cotas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Protesto_contra_o_sistema_de_cotas.jpg/255px-Protesto_contra_o_sistema_de_cotas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Protesto_contra_o_sistema_de_cotas.jpg/340px-Protesto_contra_o_sistema_de_cotas.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Protesto_contra_o_sistema_de_cotas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Students protesting against <a href="/wiki/Racial_quota" title="Racial quota">racial quotas</a> in Brazil: "<i>Quer uma vaga? Passe no vestibular!</i>" ("Do you want a spot? Pass the entrance exam!")</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Reverse_discrimination" title="Reverse discrimination">Reverse discrimination</a> is discrimination against members of a dominant or majority group, in favor of members of a minority or historically disadvantaged group. Groups may be defined in terms of <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disability</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnicity" title="Ethnicity">ethnicity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Family" title="Family">family status</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender_identity" title="Gender identity">gender identity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nationality" title="Nationality">nationality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Race_(human_categorization)" title="Race (human categorization)">race</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sex" title="Sex">sex</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a>, or other factors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (October 2020)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>This discrimination may seek to redress <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_inequalities" title="Social inequalities">social inequalities</a> under which minority groups have had less access to privileges enjoyed by the majority group. In such cases it is intended to remove discrimination that minority groups may already face. Reverse discrimination can be defined as the unequal treatment of members of the majority groups resulting from preferential policies, as in college admissions or employment, intended to remedy earlier discrimination against minorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>Conceptualizing <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> as reverse discrimination became popular in the early- to mid-1970s, a time period that focused on under-representation and action policies intended to remedy the effects of past discrimination in both government and the business world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Embrick_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Embrick-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-discrimination_legislation">Anti-discrimination legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Anti-discrimination legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_anti-discrimination_acts" title="List of anti-discrimination acts">List of anti-discrimination acts</a></div><style
