<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Racial_Discrimination_Act_1975" title="Racial Discrimination Act 1975">Racial Discrimination Act 1975</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sex_Discrimination_Act_1984" title="Sex Discrimination Act 1984">Sex Discrimination Act 1984</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Disability_Discrimination_Act_1992" title="Disability Discrimination Act 1992">Disability Discrimination Act 1992</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Age_Discrimination_Act_2004" title="Age Discrimination Act 2004">Age Discrimination Act 2004</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ontario_Human_Rights_Code" title="Ontario Human Rights Code">Ontario Human Rights Code</a> 1962</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canadian_Human_Rights_Act" title="Canadian Human Rights Act">Canadian Human Rights Act</a> 1977 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Sex Discrimination Ordinance (1996)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Prohibition_of_Discrimination_in_Products,_Services_and_Entry_into_Places_of_Entertainment_and_Public_Places_Law,_2000" title="Prohibition of Discrimination in Products, Services and Entry into Places of Entertainment and Public Places Law, 2000">Prohibition of Discrimination in Products, Services and Entry into Places of Entertainment and Public Places Law, 2000</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Employment_(Equal_Opportunities)_Law,_1988" title="Employment (Equal Opportunities) Law, 1988">Employment (Equal Opportunities) Law, 1988</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Article 137c, part 1 of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wetboek_van_Strafrecht" title="Wetboek van Strafrecht">Wetboek van Strafrecht</a> prohibits insults towards a group because of its race, religion, sexual orientation (straight or gay), handicap (somatically, mental or psychiatric) in public or by speech, by writing or by a picture. Maximum imprisonment one year of imprisonment or a fine of the third category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c3_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-c3-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></li>
<li>Part 2 increases the maximum imprisonment to two years and the maximum fine category to 4,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c4_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-c4-91">[91]</a></sup> when the crime is committed as a habit or is committed by two or more persons.</li>
<li>Article 137d prohibits provoking to discrimination or hate against the group described above. Same penalties apply as in article 137c.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li>Article 137e part 1 prohibits publishing a discriminatory statement, other than in formal message, or hands over an object (that contains discriminatory information) otherwise than on his request. Maximum imprisonment is 6 months or a fine of the third category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c3_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-c3-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li>Part 2 increases the maximum imprisonment to one year and the maximum fine category to 4,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c4_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-c4-91">[91]</a></sup> when the crime is committed as a habit or committed by two or more persons.</li>
<li>Article 137f prohibits supporting discriminatory activities by giving money or goods. Maximum imprisonment is 3 months or a fine of the second category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-c2_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-c2-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Equal_Pay_Act_1970" title="Equal Pay Act 1970">Equal Pay Act 1970</a> – provides for equal pay for comparable work.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sex_Discrimination_Act_1975" title="Sex Discrimination Act 1975">Sex Discrimination Act 1975</a> – makes discrimination against women or men, including discrimination on the grounds of marital status, illegal in the workplace.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Act_1998" title="Human Rights Act 1998">Human Rights Act 1998</a> – provides more scope for redressing all forms of discriminatory imbalances.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Equality_Act_2010" title="Equality Act 2010">Equality Act 2010</a> – consolidates, updates and supplements the prior Acts and Regulations that formed the basis of <a href="/wiki/Anti-discrimination_law" title="Anti-discrimination law">anti-discrimination law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Equal_Pay_Act_of_1963" title="Equal Pay Act of 1963">Equal Pay Act of 1963</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> – (part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fair_Labor_Standards_Act" title="Fair Labor Standards Act">Fair Labor Standards Act</a>) – prohibits wage discrimination by employers and labor organizations based on sex.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a> – many provisions, including broadly prohibiting discrimination in the workplace including hiring, firing, workforce reduction, benefits, and sexually harassing conduct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fair_Housing_Act" title="Fair Housing Act">Fair Housing Act</a> of 1968 prohibited discrimination in the sale or rental of housing based on race, color, national origin, religion, sex, familial status, or disability. The <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Fair_Housing_and_Equal_Opportunity" title="Office of Fair Housing and Equal Opportunity">Office of Fair Housing and Equal Opportunity</a> is charged with administering and enforcing the Act.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pregnancy_Discrimination_Act" title="Pregnancy Discrimination Act">Pregnancy Discrimination Act of 1978</a>, which amended Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964 – covers discrimination based upon pregnancy in the workplace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Violence_Against_Women_Act" title="Violence Against Women Act">Violence Against Women Act of 1994</a></li>
<li>Racism still occurs in a widespread manner in real estate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_documents">United Nations documents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: United Nations documents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Important UN documents addressing discrimination include:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> is a declaration adopted by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> on December 10, 1948. It states that:" <i>Everyone is entitled to all the rights and freedoms set forth in this Declaration, without distinction of any kind, such as race, colour, sex, language, religion, political or other opinion, national or social origin, property, birth or other status.</i>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/International_Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Racial_Discrimination" title="International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial Discrimination">International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial Discrimination</a> (ICERD) is a United Nations convention. The Convention commits its members to the elimination of <a href="/wiki/Racial_discrimination" title="Racial discrimination">racial discrimination</a>. The convention was adopted and opened for signature by the United Nations General Assembly on December 21, 1965, and entered into force on January 4, 1969.</li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Discrimination_against_Women" title="Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women">Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women</a> (CEDAW) is an international treaty adopted in 1979 by the United Nations General Assembly. Described as an international <a href="/wiki/Bill_of_rights" title="Bill of rights">bill of rights</a> for women, it came into force on September 3, 1981.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_Persons_with_Disabilities" title="Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities">Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities</a> is an international human rights instrument treaty of the United Nations. Parties to the convention are required to promote, protect, and ensure the full enjoyment of human rights by persons with disabilities and ensure that they enjoy full equality under the law. The text was adopted by the United Nations General Assembly on December 13, 2006, and opened for signature on March 30, 2007. Following ratification by the 20th party, it came into force on May 3, 2008.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theories_and_philosophy">Theories and philosophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Theories and philosophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_theories" title="Social theories">Social theories</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarianism</a> assert that <a href="/wiki/Social_equality" title="Social equality">social equality</a> should prevail. In some societies, including most developed countries, each individual's civil rights include the right to be free from government sponsored social discrimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Due to a belief in the capacity to perceive pain or suffering shared by all animals, <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_(animal_rights)" title="Abolitionism (animal rights)">abolitionist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Veganism" title="Veganism">vegan</a> egalitarianism maintains that the interests of every individual (regardless of their species), warrant <a href="/wiki/Equal_consideration_of_interests" title="Equal consideration of interests">equal consideration</a> with the interests of humans, and that not doing so is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speciesist" title="Speciesist">speciesist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singerethics-sentience_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-singerethics-sentience-105">[105]</a></sup>
</p><p>Philosophers have debated as to how inclusive the definition of discrimination should be. Some philosophers have argued that discrimination should only refer to wrongful or disadvantageous treatment in the context of a socially salient group (such as race, gender, sexuality etc.) within a given context. Under this view, failure to limit the concept of discrimination would lead to it being overinclusive; for example, since most murders occur because of some perceived difference between the perpetrator and the victim, many murders would constitute discrimination if the social salience requirement is not included. Thus this view argues that making the definition of discrimination overinclusive renders it meaningless. Conversely, other philosophers argue that discrimination should simply refer to wrongful disadvantageous treatment regardless of the social salience of the group, arguing that limiting the concept only to socially salient groups is arbitrary, as well as raising issues of determining which groups would count as socially salient. The issue of which groups should count has caused many political and social debates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altman_2020_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Altman_2020-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Based on realistic-conflict theory<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> and social-identity theory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Rubin and Hewstone<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> have highlighted a distinction among three types of discrimination:
</p>
<ol><li><i>Realistic competition</i> is driven by self-interest and is aimed at obtaining material resources (e.g., food, territory, customers) for the in-group (e.g., favoring an in-group in order to obtain more resources for its members, including the self).</li>
<li><i>Social competition</i> is driven by the need for self-esteem and is aimed at achieving a positive social status for the in-group relative to comparable out-groups (e.g., favoring an in-group in order to make it better than an out-group).</li>
<li><i>Consensual discrimination</i> is driven by the need for accuracy<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and reflects stable and legitimate intergroup status hierarchies (e.g., favoring a high-status in-group because it is high status).</li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labeling_theory">Labeling theory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Labeling theory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zaj%C4%99cia_Akademii_Edukacji_Antydyskryminacyjnej_w_Centrum_%C5%BBydowskim_w_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cimiu.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1133" data-file-width="1700" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Zaj%C4%99cia_Akademii_Edukacji_Antydyskryminacyjnej_w_Centrum_%C5%BBydowskim_w_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cimiu.jpg/220px-Zaj%C4%99cia_Akademii_Edukacji_Antydyskryminacyjnej_w_Centrum_%C5%BBydowskim_w_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cimiu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Zaj%C4%99cia_Akademii_Edukacji_Antydyskryminacyjnej_w_Centrum_%C5%BBydowskim_w_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cimiu.jpg/330px-Zaj%C4%99cia_Akademii_Edukacji_Antydyskryminacyjnej_w_Centrum_%C5%BBydowskim_w_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cimiu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Zaj%C4%99cia_Akademii_Edukacji_Antydyskryminacyjnej_w_Centrum_%C5%BBydowskim_w_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cimiu.jpg/440px-Zaj%C4%99cia_Akademii_Edukacji_Antydyskryminacyjnej_w_Centrum_%C5%BBydowskim_w_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cimiu.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zaj%C4%99cia_Akademii_Edukacji_Antydyskryminacyjnej_w_Centrum_%C5%BBydowskim_w_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cimiu.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An anti-discrimination education workshop at the <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_Jewish_Center_in_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cim" title="Auschwitz Jewish Center in Oświęcim">Auschwitz Jewish Center</a>, Poland, 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Discrimination, in <a href="/wiki/Labeling_theory" title="Labeling theory">labeling theory</a>, takes form as mental categorization of minorities and the use of <a href="/wiki/Stereotype" title="Stereotype">stereotype</a>. This theory describes difference as deviance from the norm, which results in internal devaluation and <a href="/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">social stigma</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> that may be seen as discrimination. It is started by describing a "natural" social order. It is distinguished between the fundamental principle of fascism and social democracy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2013)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazis" title="Nazis">Nazis</a> in 1930s-era Germany and the pre-1990 <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">Apartheid</a> government of South Africa used racially discriminatory agendas for their political ends. This practice continues with some present day governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_theory">Game theory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Game theory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Economist <a href="/wiki/Yanis_Varoufakis" title="Yanis Varoufakis">Yanis Varoufakis</a> (2013) argues that "discrimination based on utterly arbitrary characteristics evolves quickly and systematically in the experimental laboratory", and that neither classical <a href="/wiki/Game_theory" title="Game theory">game theory</a> nor <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_economics" title="Neoclassical economics">neoclassical economics</a> can explain this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2002, Varoufakis and Shaun Hargreaves-Heap ran an experiment where volunteers played a computer-mediated, multiround <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawk-dove_game" title="Hawk-dove game">hawk-dove game</a>. At the start of each session, each participant was assigned a color at random, either red or blue. At each round, each player learned the color assigned to his or her opponent, but nothing else about the opponent. Hargreaves-Heap and Varoufakis found that the players' behavior within a session frequently developed a discriminatory convention, giving a <a href="/wiki/Nash_equilibrium" title="Nash equilibrium">Nash equilibrium</a> where players of one color (the "advantaged" color) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pure_strategy" title="Pure strategy">consistently</a> played the aggressive "hawk" strategy against players of the other, "disadvantaged" color, who played the acquiescent "dove" strategy against the advantaged color. Players of both colors used a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_strategy" title="Mixed strategy">mixed strategy</a> when playing against players assigned the same color as their own. The experimenters then added a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisoners%27_dilemma" title="Prisoners' dilemma">cooperation</a> option to the game, and found that disadvantaged players usually cooperated with each other, while advantaged players usually did not. They state that while the equilibria reached in the original hawk-dove game are predicted by <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_game_theory" title="Evolutionary game theory">evolutionary game theory</a>, game theory does not explain the emergence of cooperation in the disadvantaged group. Citing earlier psychological work of <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Rabin" title="Matthew Rabin">Matthew Rabin</a>, they hypothesize that a norm of differing entitlements emerges across the two groups, and that this norm could define a "fairness" equilibrium within the disadvantaged group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="State_vs._free_market">State vs. free market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: State vs. free market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>It is debated as to whether or not <a href="/wiki/Market_(economics)" title="Market (economics)">markets</a> discourage discrimination brought about by the state. One argument is that since discrimination restricts access to customers and incurs additional expense, market logic will punish discrimination. Opposition by companies to "Jim Crow" segregation laws is an example of this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roback_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-roback-113">[113]</a></sup> An alternative argument is that markets don't necessarily undermine discrimination, as it is argued that if discrimination is profitable by catering to the "<a href="/wiki/Taste-based_discrimination" title="Taste-based discrimination">tastes</a>" of individuals (which is the point of the market), then the market will not punish discrimination. It is argued that micro economic analysis of discrimination uses unusual methods to determine its effects (using explicit treatment of production functions) and that the very existence of discrimination in employment (defined as wages which differ from marginal product of the discriminated employees) in the long run contradicts claims that the market will function well and punish discrimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Furthermore, economic actors may have imperfect information and <a href="/wiki/Statistical_discrimination_(economics)" title="Statistical discrimination (economics)">statistical discrimination</a> may occur rationally and without prejudice.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discrimination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFAltman2020">Altman, Andrew (2020), <a class="external text" href="https://plato.stanford.edu/archives/sum2020/entries/discrimination/" rel="nofollow">"Discrimination"</a>,  in Zalta, Edward N. (ed.), <i><a href="/wiki/Stanford_Encyclopedia_of_Philosophy" title="Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy">Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy</a></i> (Summer 2020 ed.), Metaphysics Research Lab, Stanford University<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">October 13,</span> 2020</span>, <q>[A]s a reasonable first approximation, we can say that discrimination consists of acts, practices, or policies that impose a relative disadvantage on persons based on their membership in a salient social group. [...] [W]e can refine the first-approximation account of discrimination and say that the moralized concept of discrimination is properly applied to acts, practices or policies that meet two conditions: a) they wrongfully impose a relative disadvantage or deprivation on persons based on their membership in some salient social group, and b) the wrongfulness rests (in part) on the fact that the imposition of the disadvantage is on account of the group membership of the victims.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Discrimination&amp;rft.btitle=Stanford+Encyclopedia+of+Philosophy&amp;rft.edition=Summer+2020&amp;rft.pub=Metaphysics+Research+Lab%2C+Stanford+University&amp;rft.date=2020&amp;rft.aulast=Altman&amp;rft.aufirst=Andrew&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fplato.stanford.edu%2Farchives%2Fsum2020%2Fentries%2Fdiscrimination%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADiscrimination"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-Lenhart-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Lenhart_64-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Lenhart_64-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFSharyn_Ann_Lenhart2004">Sharyn Ann Lenhart (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Rt2SAgAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA6" rel="nofollow"><i>Clinical Aspects of Sexual Harassment and Gender Discrimination: Psychological Consequences and Treatment Interventions</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>. p. 6. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1135941314" title="Special:BookSources/978-1135941314"><bdi>978-1135941314</bdi></a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">April 20,</span> 2018</span>. <q>GENDER OR SEX DISCRIMINATION: This term refers to the types of gender bias that have a negative impact. The term has legal, as well as theoretical and psychological, definitions. Psychological consequences can be more readily inferred from the latter, but both definitions are of significance. Theoretically, gender discrimination has been described as (1) the unequal rewards that men and women receive in the workplace or academic environment because of their gender or sex difference (DiThomaso, 1989); (2) a process occurring in work or educational settings in which an individual is overtly or covertly limited access to an opportunity or a resource because of a sex or is given the opportunity or the resource reluctantly and may face harassment for picking it (Roeske &amp; Pleck, 1983); or (3) both.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Clinical+Aspects+of+Sexual+Harassment+and+Gender+Discrimination%3A+Psychological+Consequences+and+Treatment+Interventions&amp;rft.pages=6&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-1135941314&amp;rft.au=Sharyn+Ann+Lenhart&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DRt2SAgAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA6&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADiscrimination"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-singerethics-sentience-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-singerethics-sentience_105-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFSinger1999"><a href="/wiki/Peter_Singer" title="Peter Singer">Singer, Peter</a> (1999) [1993]. This is why the limit of sentience ... is the only defensible boundary of concern for the interests of others. ... <li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-112">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation cs2" id="CITEREFShaun_Hargreaves-HeapYanis_Varoufakis2002">Shaun Hargreaves-Heap; Yanis Varoufakis (July 2002), "Some experimental evidence on the evolution of discrimination, co-operation and perceptions of fairness", <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economic_Journal" title="The Economic Journal">The Economic Journal</a></i>, <b>112</b> (481): 679–703, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1111%2F1468-0297.00735" rel="nofollow">10.1111/1468-0297.00735</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:59133304" rel="nofollow">59133304</a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Economic+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=Some+experimental+evidence+on+the+evolution+of+discrimination%2C+co-operation+and+perceptions+of+fairness&amp;rft.volume=112&amp;rft.issue=481&amp;rft.pages=679-703&amp;rft.date=2002-07&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1111%2F1468-0297.00735&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A59133304%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.au=Shaun+Hargreaves-Heap&amp;rft.au=Yanis+Varoufakis&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADiscrimination"></span></span>
